Bandit Liu Raids Shaanzhou 122

County Magistrate of Lingbao Pleads for Help

Kaifeng Correspondence: Liu Guitang's bandit troops arrived at Yaikou Village, in the jurisdiction of Luoning County, at 11:00 AM on the 17th of this month, only fifteen li from the city. County Magistrate Qin Shuo, intimidated by the bandit forces, led the Fifth District Militia defending the city and retreated to the south bank of the Luo River. The county security team also left the city and took refuge on the northern mountains. The bandit troops then entered the city safely that night, raping, killing, looting at will. On the morning of the 18th, Tang Junde's troops arrived, and the bandits broke through the encirclement and scattered to the southwest of Lushi and the northwest of Shaanzhou. Caoyuan Town, Zhangbian Town, and other places were disturbed. Zhang Fang, the commander-in-chief of the 20th Route Army, being a native of Xin'an and familiar with the terrain, was ordered to the front to supervise the suppression. He arrived at Guanyintang yesterday (the 21st). Gao Jianbai's troops of the 21st Brigade of the 84th Division stationed in Zhengzhou were also ordered to set out for western Henan today to participate in the bandit suppression. This morning, according to a telegram from Ouyang Zhen, the commissioner of the 11th District of Shaanzhou, Liu's bandits had passed through Yanling Pass and reached Zhangcun Xinzhuang near Guanqian, about forty li from the city, and continued to flee westward. He requested that armored vehicles be sent quickly between Shaanzhou and Lingbao to block them. At the same time, Sun Chunrong, the county magistrate of Lingbao, also telegraphed that Liu's bandits were threatening to attack Lingbao, causing panic among merchants and residents. In addition to deploying security and militia teams to attack decisively at key points, he requested that a large army be sent to Lingbao to suppress them. The panic that had gripped northern Henan a few days ago has now shifted to western Henan. He Zhuguo, who was previously responsible for suppressing Liu's bandits in northern Henan, and Gao Guizi, the commander of the 84th Division, came to Bian yesterday to meet Liu Shi and report on the bandit suppression. They stayed at Weigong Bank, a mountain goods store, and He left Bian to return to his defense today (February 22nd).

Second Phase of Bandit Suppression Begins in Southern Route Army 123

Generals Return to their Posts One After Another

Blockade of Bandit Areas Shows Results

Guangzhou Communication: Some days ago, Yu Hanmou, the commander of the First Army and commander of the First Column of the Southern Route Bandit Suppression Army, returned to Guangdong to discuss the second phase of the plan to suppress the communist bandits in Jiangxi Province. He held several meetings with Chen Jitang to discuss specific measures. At the same time, the deputy division commanders of the various divisions on the front line in southern Jiangxi also successively returned to the province to report on the military situation at the front. The military meetings have now concluded, and the generals have left the province and returned to their defense posts. Yu Hanmou also returned from the province to his hometown of Zhaoqing in western Guangdong yesterday, staying for a day or two before returning to Dageng to preside over the suppression of the communist bandits. Therefore, in recent days, the various troops in southern Jiangxi have been preparing everything. It is reported that in this communist suppression plan, the entire First Column will be sent to eastern Jiangxi, uniting with the Central Army to encircle the bandit areas on a large scale, with the aim of eliminating the remaining communist bandits in Jiangxi in a short period of time. In recent days, Li Zhenqiu's First Division of the First Army, stationed in Nankang, has sent a part of its troops to strengthen the frontline forces. The Teaching Regiment of the Second Division, originally stationed in An Yuan Chongshi Xu, is responsible for searching for the remaining bandits in the front. At 5:00 AM on the 13th of this month, it sent two battalions of soldiers, together with the Second Battalion of the Fifth Regiment, to the vicinity of Heshi to search for and suppress communist bandits who were extorting rice from the people. The farmers in the area were forced to hand over three dou and two sheng of rice per person by the communist bandits, and several hundred shi had already been extorted. The farmers dared to be angry but dared not speak out. Fortunately, the government troops arrived, detected the location of the bandits, and surrounded them without making a sound. The communist bandits and pseudo-guerrillas fled in panic towards Heshi. Numerous bandits were killed on the spot by the government troops, and 300 shi of rice looted by the communist bandits were intercepted and transported back to Chongshi Xu for disposal. The defense troops, knowing that the communist bandits were short of food, have now delineated a blockade line for the bandit areas in southern Jiangxi, strictly blockading it to cut off the supply of food, salt, medicine, and other materials to the communist bandits. The entire blockade line is divided into three sections. In addition to the defense troops stepping up patrols within the line, the militia groups, communist eradication groups, and agency teams within the section must also cooperate to achieve the effect of cooperation between the government and the people. It is estimated that since the implementation of the blockade of the bandit areas, a considerable amount of food, salt, and medicine smuggled by the communist bandits has been intercepted. The Second Division and Fourth Division have successively captured about 500 communist bandits and seized more than 300 machine guns. The remaining bandits are mostly deeply hidden in Huichang and Ruijin. Only a few local communists are active above An Yuan. (February 20th)

Increased Fees for Shipping Donations in Chao Shan 124

Shantou Communication: The automotive transportation on land in Chao Shan has been quite developed recently, and the business of coastal and inland river electric boats and steamships has been greatly impacted. In addition, the market is cold and freight volume has sharply decreased. The Chao Shan Port Authority recently announced a new chapter on the quarterly dues levied on electric boats and steamships, which is more than doubled compared to the previous one. Those sailing on the Shantou Yangyang Huanggang Shanwei lines used to pay 113 yuan per year, totaling only 400 yuan per year. Now it has increased to 900 yuan per year. The Shantou Chaoyang Dahao route used to pay 907 yuan per quarter, totaling 300 yuan per year. Now the annual fee has increased to 800 yuan. The various ships sailing on the Chaoan Dapu Songkou lines used to pay 75 yuan per quarter, totaling 300 yuan per year. Now it has increased to 600 yuan. The small electric boats on the inland rivers of Chaoyang Lianjiang and Jieyang Mianhu Fugang Tangkeng Yuyao Zhongtang used to pay 37 yuan per quarter, totaling 100 yuan per year. Now it has also increased to 312 yuan. At the end of the lunar year, the Chao Shan Wheel Electric Association specially petitioned the provincial government to establish a building hall, requesting exemption to maintain transportation, but it has not yet been approved. As a result, since the new year, most of the company's electric boats have been suspended.

Songjiang - The Slump in the Rice Market Affects All Industries 125

Songjiang is a rice-producing area. The rice market is concentrated in three locations: Xitan, Da Zhangjing, and Dongmen. Xitan has the largest business in the rice market, followed by Da Zhangjing. The annual total is more than 400,000 to 500,000 dan. However, rice prices have been low for many years, and rice operators often hear of losses. At the end of last year, several companies suffered excessive losses and went bankrupt. There were seven bankruptcies in Xitan and one in Dongmen, Wanchang Rice Store. Due to the impact of the rice market, the following businesses went bankrupt: Dongmen Shuntaiyi Lumber Store, and four old stores on West Avenue, Tong Jinchang Cai Zhang Yuan Fengchang Zhang. They are all old stores that have been in business for many years, but they are unwilling to continue operating due to years of losses. This is enough to show the sluggishness of Songjiang's business.

Wuxi - Active Construction of the Huanhu Highway 128

County Magistrate Yan and Rong Desheng and Yu Xunzheng from the western township are planning to develop a lakeside road to improve the lakeside scenery. The technical department of the county government has completed the survey of the entire route and the two branch roads of Yuantouzhu and Xiaojishan. The Huanhu Road is 11 kilometers and 89 meters long, the Yuantouzhu branch road is more than 600 meters long, and the Xiaojishan branch road is more than 100 meters long. All waterways and the horizontal line of the Zhongdu Mountain section have also been surveyed. Construction is scheduled to begin within days. The most important part of the entire road construction is the bridge project. A long levee will be built between Baishizui and Sujiazui, connected by bridges, to make the road circular. When the road construction is completed in the future, the scenery will not be inferior to the Su Causeway, Bai Causeway, the Six Bridges, and the Three Temples.

Yangzhou - Provincial Order to Investigate Illegal Construction 131

Ji Naizhen, the principal of the 江都 County Middle School, illegally constructed a school building. Citizens Zou Fengming and Sun Baoqin believed that he had arbitrarily started the project and misappropriated huge sums of money, and they separately filed complaints with the Provincial Government Construction Department. The Provincial Government has now received a joint report from the Construction and Education Departments on this case and specially ordered the 江都 County Government, stating that the county middle school had allocated a large amount of money for the construction of the school building without first submitting the drawings and detailed accounts of the project to the Education Department for approval before allocating the funds. The principal also failed to supervise the contracting craftsmen to obtain licenses in accordance with the regulations before starting construction, which were all inappropriate. It should be reprimanded together. Since it has been reported that the construction project of the school is urgently needed, in addition to ordering the county magistrate to order the supplementary issuance of licenses in accordance with the construction regulations of the province, the construction drawings and detailed accounts of the project should also be submitted for review. The county government has now complied with the order and transferred it to the Education Bureau for handling. Yesterday (the 22nd), the plaintiffs Zou Fengming and Sun Baoqin had recorded the approval order of the Provincial Government and submitted it to the county, requesting that it be handled in accordance with the regulations and that the case be investigated and punished.

Nantong - Settlement of Aviation Lottery Lawsuit 132

Yang Youheng, director of the Liu Haisha Public Security Branch, received a fifth prize, number 227404, for 200 yuan, for the third phase of the aviation lottery from the Bank of China in Nantong. Seven days later, the Bank of China returned the lottery ticket with the number 227104 altered. Yang denied that the ticket was altered and claimed it was the original. He filed a criminal complaint with the Nantong Court against Yu Chongwei, the president of the Bank of China, for embezzling the prize money. On the 23rd, prosecutor Wang Lansheng summoned all the witnesses from both sides for interrogation. The Ministry of Finance also sent Zhao Xianglu to Nantong to appear in court. Later, the plaintiff and defendant both accepted the mediation of local people and were unwilling to litigate. The Bank of China paid Yang Youheng 200 yuan, and Yang withdrew the lawsuit in court.

Xiaoshan - Salt Boat Sinks, Seven Drowned 133

A resident of Hengcha Town in the Seventh District of Xiaoshan, Lu Yongxiang's son, A Quan, and seven neighbors, including Shao and Li, loaded two boats full of salt, intending to sell it in Jiangbei. Unfortunately, due to overloading and the impact of the raging tide, the boat shook. Unexpectedly, when they sailed to Nan Shantou in Wuli, the sky was already dark and the wind suddenly became stronger. The high tide hit the boat, and the entire boat capsized. All seven people on board drowned. When the sand people saw empty boats floating on the river and clothing items left inside the boat, they realized that the seven people had been killed by the wind. Now, the families of the Lu, Shao, and Li families are trying their best to salvage, but only one corpse has been recovered, and the rest are still missing.

[PICTURE DESCRIPTION] Photo six of the Southern Xinjiang organization's puppet government.

Impressionistic Notes on an Economic Survey of Guangxi Province (Part 1) by Qian Jiaju 134

This time, at the invitation of the Guangxi Provincial Government, we went to Guangxi Province to investigate the province's economic situation. The trip lasted six months. We are deeply grateful for the warm hospitality of the provincial authorities. The materials obtained are currently being organized, and a Guangxi economic survey report will be submitted and officially published by the Social Survey Institute soon. Now, I will record my personal observations and feelings during the journey, hoping to provide some reference for those who are concerned about the construction problems of Guangxi Province."

Guangxi is a province in the southwestern border area, with an area of ​​over 84,000 square miles and a population of approximately 12 million. Because its southwestern corner is adjacent to French Annam, it occupies a very important position in national defense. However, due to its remote location and obstructed transportation, it is naturally more backward than Jiangsu, Zhejiang and other provinces in terms of its economy or culture. However, since the cooperation between Guangdong and Guangxi twenty years ago, the authorities of the province have been able to diligently seek governance and work hard on construction after the military devastation. In a short period of time, remarkable achievements have been made. For a time, the title of "New Guangxi" was well-known throughout the country, and the economy, politics, and construction of Guangxi Province have gradually attracted the attention of the people across the country. This time, we were invited by the provincial authorities to conduct an economic survey of the entire province to provide a reference for Guangxi's future economic construction. We have long admired the landscape of Guilin, which is known as the best in the world. Secondly, we felt that it was worth visiting such a new province. Therefore, we happily accepted the order and decided to depart from Beiping in early July of last year. Before departure, we started various preparations for the survey, such as collecting records of political and economic problems in Guangxi from various newspapers and magazines, and collecting economic survey forms from various academic institutions. My colleagues were Mr. Wu Bannong and Mr. Han Dezhang, and myself. Because I had some personal matters to go back to my hometown in Zhejiang, I set off from Beiping on June 20 and stayed in Wuyi for a week. I returned to Shanghai on July 5. It happened that at this time, Mr. Wu and Mr. Han also came to Shanghai from Beiping. After contacting Mr. Huang Jianping, the Guangxi representative in Shanghai, we immediately purchased second-class tickets for the Italian postal ship "Conte Verde" which departed on July 14. The fare for the ship to Hong Kong was 97 yuan and 60 cents. At the same time, Mr. Huang Jianping telegraphed our itinerary to Mr. Li Baihuang. Mr. Wu and Mr. Han heard from Mr. Zhang Xinyi in Nanjing that the climate in Guangxi Province was warm and hot, and there were many seasonal diseases and miasma. In order to prevent problems before they occurred, we got vaccinated against cholera and typhoid fever before leaving Shanghai. We also purchased a large number of medicines, such as quinine, ten drops of water, and Jizhong water. After everything was arranged, we boarded the ship at 9:00 am on the 14th. At 1:00 pm, the crew sailed from the Pudong Wharf. When she left this prosperous and tense city, our hearts felt extraordinarily relaxed, but when we thought that she was carrying us further away from Beiping, we felt a little melancholy. The Italian Post is a rising star in the Euro-Asian route, especially the second-class cabin of Conte Verde, which is said to be originally a part of the first-class cabin and is specially designed for "higher-class Chinese" to ride. Therefore, the cabins are elegant and comfortably furnished, and the Saloon is especially magnificent. After boarding the ship, we realized that there was also a second-class economy cabin, which cost only 60 yuan to Hong Kong.

We didn't buy the economy class this time, which was really a bit bourgeois.

On the ship, Mr. Zhang introduced us to Mr. Lei Binnan, the current Director of Education of Guangxi Province. Mr. Lei is a well-known popular educator in China's education circle, and also a senior in the revolutionary circle. In the Smoking Room, he and we painfully discussed the shortcomings of the Chinese education system, which only cultivated a group of higher-class idlers who have nothing to do with social production. This time, the highest authorities in Guangxi originally asked Mr. Lei to be the Director of Education, but his own plan was to return to Guangxi to establish a National Production Education College (the name is yet to be determined). Mr. Lei expressed warm welcome to our economic survey work, because when the first administrative meeting of Guangxi was held last year, he first proposed that Guangxi should establish an economic committee. The initial work of the committee was to conduct field surveys, and then make a plan for the economic construction of the province based on the survey materials. Therefore, the help and guidance we received from Mr. Lei along the way and after arriving in Guangxi was indeed not insignificant.

The time on the ship passed quickly in conversation or looking into the distance. At 5:00 pm on the second day, there was also music in the second-class Saloon. According to Mr. Han Dezhang (who is proficient in music), Suauss's Enjoy Life Verde Ajda and Moskowsky's Spanish Dances were all famous songs, but unfortunately I am a genuine layman, which is really no different from "playing the lute to a cow." At 9:00 pm, there was also a sound movie, titled Terra Madre (Mother Earth), but the film was not very good, and the language was Italian, so I couldn't understand the plot. Before the end of the show, we went back to the room to sleep. After waking up and washing up, and tidying up our luggage, Hong Kong was already vaguely visible. We had read Lu Xun's experience of passing through Hong Kong before, knowing that when going ashore in Hong Kong, there are special high-class nationals who check the luggage of Chinese people. If you don't bribe them with money, they may turn your suitcase upside down or poke seven holes in it. This time, we brought a lot of luggage, and we couldn't help but feel uneasy, so we asked in advance how much gift each piece of luggage had to pay to the inspectors, so as not to be at a loss when the time came. At this time, Mr. Huang Xianru told us that if there was too much luggage, there was also a way to avoid the trouble of the inspectors, that is, to let someone stay at the Hongkong Hotel for one night, because the tea boys who serve guests at the Hongkong Hotel are blue-eyed and only need to hand over the luggage to him, and you will not be inspected, because inspection has always been applied only to compatriots. This is indeed a clever way, but because we had already decided to stay at the Queen's Hotel, and the room rate at the Hongkong Hotel was too expensive, it was inconvenient to live separately, so we didn't do that. At 12:00 noon, the ship docked at the Royal Wharf. At this time, a large number of coolies (dockworkers) swarmed in, their momentum was fierce, as if facing a battlefield. None of the three of us could speak Cantonese, fortunately, Mr. Lei Binnan came to greet us. After a lot of talking, we spent more than six yuan in total for inspection fees and porterage fees, and finally got the luggage safely moved to the Queen's Hotel. After the room was settled, we took Mr. Huang Jianping's letter of introduction to the Hong Kong Guangxi Bank to see Mr. Zeng Qixin and Mr. Zhang Zhaotang, the president and vice president. Who knew that today was just a Sunday and the bank was closed. After waiting for a long time, we finally invited Mr. Zhang, the vice president. However, Mr. Zhang did not seem to understand the task of our trip, and only said, "Commander-in-chief Li is also in Hong Kong. Would you like to meet him?" Of course we wanted to meet Mr. Li, so we asked Mr. Zhang to arrange a time to meet Mr. Li and notify us by phone at night. After coming out of the Guangxi Bank, we went to see Mr. Li Feng, a friend introduced to us by Mr. Chen Junhui, a colleague of our bank. Mr. Li is the manager of the Yong Coffee Company (in Hong Kong, managers are called "Sili"). He treated us very sincerely. He said that the next day was the date of their company's delivery, and he couldn't spare time to accompany us, so he wanted to entrust a friend from the Youth Association, Mr. Liu, to be our guide for touring Hong Kong. After returning to the hotel, we received a call from Manager Zhang at night, saying that he had arranged to meet Mr. Li at his home at 7:00 am the next morning.

An interesting thing happened at the Queen's Hotel. At 8:00 or 9:00 pm, a tea boy ran in and asked one of our colleagues if he wanted to smoke opium. Our colleague shook his head, and he walked away dejectedly. After a while, he poked his head in again. We asked him what he was doing. He said, "Do you gentlemen want to call a girl to relieve boredom?" We gave him another cold shoulder. From then on, the waiter's response was no longer responsive and the service was also simplified. We naturally had to listen to it. The situation of Hong Kong hotels can also be imagined in general.

Belgian Envoy to Hold Memorial Service for Former King Tomorrow 135

Belgian Envoy Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday to Preside Over the Service

To Be Held in Nanjing Next Wednesday

Inviting All Circles, Chinese and Foreign, to Attend

Since King Albert I of Belgium tragically died while hiking, people all over the world have been shocked and mourned. Belgian Envoy to China, Mr. Guillaume de Lichtervelde, rushed south from Beiping and arrived in Shanghai last night at 11:00 pm. It is scheduled to hold a memorial service at the St. Joseph's Church in the French Concession at 11:30 am tomorrow (the 26th). At that time, our country's authorities and foreign envoys will attend. The details of each situation are recorded as follows:

Belgian Envoy Arrived in Shanghai Last Night: The Belgian Envoy, Mr. Guillaume de Lichtervelde and his wife, were extremely saddened after learning of the shocking news of the Belgian King. On the one hand, they telegraphed the Consul-General in Shanghai to prepare for holding a memorial service in Shanghai. On the other hand, they immediately packed their luggage and went south. They took the Shanghai-Beiping train from Beiping on the morning of the 23rd and passed through Nanjing yesterday afternoon. They arrived at the North Railway Station at 11:00 pm. Personnel from the Belgian Consulate in Shanghai all went to the station to welcome them. After the Belgian Envoy got off the train, he went to his residence on Rue Lafayette to rest.

Memorial Ceremony Scheduled: The Belgian Envoy has decided to hold a memorial service for the late King at St. Joseph's Church on Rue de la Cathédrale at 11:30 am tomorrow. The memorial ceremony will be a religious memorial Mass. It is heard that the procedures have been arranged as follows: Playing the Belgian national anthem, the Belgian Father, Dean of the P'u Ai Church, will be the celebrant, assisted by the Franciscan Jesuit Father Ke. After the main sacrifice, there will be a grand memorial service. The celebrant will be the Archbishop of Shanghai, Huida. During the offering of sacrifices, the Lord Mother Society will sing the scriptures. The chapel will be ready tomorrow morning. The positions of the sacrificers are: right - the Belgian Envoy and the Belgian Consul, etc., left - our country's representatives and foreign envoys or representatives. Behind the false coffin are the Belgian expatriates. In front of the statue is the distinguished guests from all countries and all walks of life. It is also known that the Belgian Embassy has notified the personnel of the embassies and consulates in China that they will all wear mourning clothes for three months to express their condolences.

Foreign Envoys Participate: The foreign envoys and diplomatic personnel in Shanghai learned that the Belgian Envoy had scheduled to hold a memorial service for the late Belgian King in Shanghai, so they signed up with the Consulate-General to participate. As of noon yesterday, more than 200 people had signed up. Wu Tiecheng, the Mayor of Shanghai, and Yu Ming, the Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, have notified the Belgian Consulate that they will participate on time. The Belgian Embassy in Nanjing will hold a memorial service on the morning of the 28th, so Mr. Guillaume de Lichtervelde is scheduled to enter Nanjing on the 27th to preside over the service.

Notice from the Belgian Embassy: A notice issued by the Belgian Embassy states: "In order to mourn the late Belgian King Albert, the Belgian Envoy to China, Mr. Guillaume de Lichtervelde, has specifically scheduled to hold a memorial Mass at the Catholic Cathedral in Nanjing at 11:30 am on Wednesday, the 28th of this month. Chinese government officials, foreign personnel stationed in China, friends, and ladies from all walks of life are respectfully invited to attend the memorial service and share the sacrifice. This notice serves as an invitation card. It is hoped that you will understand the original intention and be fortunate."

Song Ziwen Talks About the Silver Agreement 136

Stabilizing Silver Prices is the Same as the Current Situation

Reducing Orders for American Cotton is Currently Under Negotiation

Mr. Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council, received reporters from various newspapers at the office of the Economic Council on West Yanan Road yesterday morning and made important remarks on various issues such as silver. He said that the silver agreement does not violate social psychology, and expressed that he himself will enter Nanjing next week, and plans to go to the Northwest with Dai Jitao next month. As for the American cotton and wheat loan, the amount of cotton loan will be reduced as much as possible. The details of Mr. Song's remarks are recorded as follows:

The Situation and Psychology Change Very Quickly: Regarding the silver issue, Mr. Song said that in the past three or four years, its price has fluctuated greatly. Three or four years ago, its decline was the most severe. At that time, the general public thought that silver had been abandoned internationally and had no way out, so it flooded into China. Therefore, some people advocated banning the import of silver. Recently, the price of silver has shown an increasing trend, so some people advocated banning the export of silver. The situations before and after are completely opposite. I am afraid that the most vocal advocates of banning the export of silver now may also be the most vocal advocates of banning the import of silver before. The speed of changes in the situation and psychology is so rapid.

The Origin of the Silver Agreement: As for the purpose of the London Silver Agreement, it is to stabilize silver prices, which is already known to the people of the country. The biggest reason for the sharp drop in silver prices a few years ago was that India abandoned the silver standard and sold a huge amount of silver to the international market. According to last year's statistics, India still has 400 million ounces of silver after abolishing the silver standard. At the same time, Spain also has a large amount of silver circulating in the market. Therefore, the silver agreement stipulates that India, Spain, and other countries that have changed from the silver standard to the gold standard shall not sell more than 35 million ounces of silver each year. At the same time, silver-producing countries such as Mexico, the United States, and Canada shall each purchase 35 million ounces of silver from the national treasury each year. China shall also not sell the silver stored in the government treasury to the market in order to balance the supply of silver and stabilize silver prices. The general public now hopes that our country's silver will not flow out. The London Silver Agreement is based on this meaning, so it does not violate social psychology.

Unwilling to Criticize Countermeasures: As for the amount of silver owned by China, it is not much. In addition to the hard currency preserved by the Central Bank, there is no so-called national treasury silver. What is referred to in the agreement is that in the future, or after our country changes to the gold standard, if there is excess silver, it will flow out to foreign countries. As for the recent reminting of silver coins in the United States and the statements of the banking industry, the government will naturally have competent authorities to decide on major policies. As the former Minister of Finance, I am reluctant to make any criticisms or speculations due to my position.

The Purpose of the Previously Promulgated Silver Tax: As for the issue of levying a silver export tax, Mr. Song only stated that the purpose of the previously promulgated 2.25% silver export tax was purely to add a minting fee of 2.25% to the value of the national standard silver currency after the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan, in addition to the pure silver content. Foreign merchants are unwilling to use silver coins, but still use silver taels, because silver taels have no minting fee burden, which is relatively cost-effective. Therefore, it is stipulated that silver taels are subject to export tax, while silver coins are exempt, in order to unify their value, make the national currency flow smoothly, and unify the currency system, without any intention of restricting silver exports.

Negotiating to Reduce American Cotton Quota: Subsequently, reporters inquired about the American cotton and wheat loan. The contract stipulated 40 million US dollars for American cotton. It is heard that only more than 6 million gold yuan have been shipped to our country, and the balance is still as high as more than 30 million yuan. Our country's market situation does not have such a large purchasing power. How will the original loan contract be modified? Mr. Song replied that when the loan contract was signed last year, our country's yarn mills had a large demand for American cotton. Later, due to the bumper harvest of cotton in our country last year, the demand for foreign cotton was greatly reduced, resulting in failure to purchase according to the contract. We are currently discussing with American merchants to reduce the quantity. The detailed amount is still under negotiation, roughly based on the needs of our country's market. Reporters also asked whether the cotton quota would be used to purchase other goods after the reduction. Mr. Song did not answer.

Entering Nanjing Next Week and Going to the Northwest: Mr. Song continued, regarding the allocation of business expenses of the National Economic Council, I went to Hangzhou last time and exchanged opinions in detail with General Jiang. Next week, I will go to Nanjing to discuss with Mr. Wang Jingwei, Sun Zhesheng, and Kong Yongzhi again before a decision can be made. In the Northwest, in Shaanxi and Gansu provinces, the Economic Council is planning to engage in construction projects such as developing water conservancy and building roads. I recently want to go to Shaanxi and Gansu to see their economic situation as a basis for engaging in economic construction. Mr. Dai Jitao, President of the Examination Yuan, is very enthusiastic about developing the Northwest and plans to travel with him to inspect Shaanxi and Gansu in the middle of next month. After inspecting Shaanxi and Gansu, he also plans to go to Sichuan, because the Sichuan and Shaanxi provinces occupy an important position in the future revival of our country's economic construction.

Should an Export Tax Be Levied After the United States Raises Silver Prices? 137

Shanghai's Financial Circles Are Also Divided

Those Who Advocate Tax Collection: A reporter from the Central News Agency learned yesterday morning that the US government's reminting of silver coins and efforts to raise silver prices are of great importance to the interests of our country. They specifically inquired with financial circles in Shanghai about the benefits and harms that our country will experience after silver prices rise. Our country is a silver standard country. The rise in silver prices will invisibly increase the amount of wealth in our country. This is an inevitable trend. Moreover, our country has a huge amount of foreign debt. The exchange rate at the time of repayment of foreign debt varies greatly depending on the price of silver. This is the benefit that our country can experience after silver prices rise. Other benefits, such as the ability of our country's merchants to take advantage of this good opportunity to compete for the export of domestic goods after silver prices rise, are also not insignificant. As for its harm, it is a hundred times greater than this. After silver prices rise, the outflow of silver is inevitable and there is no way to prevent it. Since the US government announced its plan to raise silver prices, the Shanghai banking community has telegraphed US President Roosevelt to state its opinions, but has not yet received a reply. However, it is expected that this plan of the US government is likely to be implemented. A telegram from Shanghai's banking community may be of little use. Therefore, the most important task now is to plan what methods to use to stop the domestic outflow of silver once the US government implements its plan to raise silver prices. There is really no other way than to levy an export tax on silver. As for the regulation of the tax rate, it should be increased or decreased at any time. For example, if the silver price increases by 20%, then the tax rate must also be increased to 20% so that silver transporters have no profit to be made. It is also necessary to stipulate that those who smuggle silver for export should be punished with extreme penalties. However, it is feared that the export of silver cannot be completely prohibited. Our country is an importing country and must use silver to order foreign goods. As for someone saying that domestic prices can also be raised after silver prices rise, this is enough to harm ourselves, because the economic panic in China has reached its peak, purchasing power is weak, resulting in stockpiles of goods, and the decline of the rural economy is in urgent need of relief. Raising prices will put all industries in the country in a more difficult situation.

Those Who Doubt Tax Collection: Xin Sheng News Agency reported that since the banking community in Shanghai expressed opposition to the US policy of raising silver prices, all parties have expressed their opinions except for the government authorities, who have expressed their consideration. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency quoted a banker yesterday as saying that US President Roosevelt's purpose of raising silver prices is actually one of the policies of the recovery plan to relieve unemployment. Therefore, the opposition from Shanghai's banking community is only to express our country's attitude in order to attract their attention. If it is said that this telegram can make the United States change its policy, there is actually no such possibility. Therefore, the majority of the US President in Congress has approved the implementation of this policy. Under this situation, the telegram from our country's silver community is inconvenient to express its attitude, so Mr. Roosevelt is unlikely to reply. As for our country's countermeasures, some advocate levying a silver export tax to show resistance, but the silver itself fluctuates up and down with the market price at any time and has no fixed price, so it cannot be the same as other tax collection methods. It is impossible to determine the tax rate as a percentage. Therefore, even if there is a possibility of implementation, it cannot be done without detailed research because the difficulty lies in the complexity. However, in terms of the US raising silver prices, the impact on our country is also bound to be very profound. Our country's biggest shortcoming is that production is backward. The US raising silver prices is to suppress its freight prices in order to find a way out for its surplus production. Our country has always been a exporting country, exchanging goods for goods, so how can silver flow out? In recent years, even the only two major exports of silk and tea have been in decline, so the only way to remedy the situation in the future is to hope for political stability and strive to increase production.

Denies Holding Emergency Meeting

The Shanghai Evening Post reported that the Shanghai American Chamber of Commerce held an emergency meeting yesterday (23rd) to discuss the silver issue and resolved to telegraph President Roosevelt to request careful handling. According to an official of the Chamber of Commerce, the meeting yesterday afternoon was a routine annual meeting and not an emergency meeting. Shanghai-Guangdong: Two Round-Trips Each Week

Wuhan-Chongqing: Three Round-Trips Each Week

The Shanghai-Guangdong route is scheduled to resume its original flights on March 2. At the same time, the Wuhan-Chongqing route is scheduled to increase flights on March 5. The company's announcement of the changes to the flight schedules of the two routes is recorded in the following table:

Shanghai-Guangdong Route: The company previously ordered a new aircraft from the United States for use on the Shanghai-Guangdong route, and it has now been assembled. It is now scheduled to change the flights on this route to two round-trips each week, starting on March 2. Wuhan-Chongqing Route: The company has found that passengers and mail on the Wuhan-Chongqing route have been extremely crowded recently, causing passengers to often miss out. In order to meet the needs of all parties, it has specially increased the flights on this route to three round-trips each week, starting on March 5. Li Jingcong Returns to Shanghai to Talk About the Test Flight on the Beiping-Shaanxi Route 140

Decides to Start Flights Next Month

Mr. Li Jingcong, Manager of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, flew from Shanghai to Beiping on the 5th of this month to test fly the Beiping-Shaanxi route. He flew from Beiping to Taiyuan on the 19th, arrived in Xi'an on the 21st, and went to Hankou via Xiangyang and Fancheng on the 22nd. At around 10:00 am the day before yesterday, he returned from Hubei and passed through Nanjing at around 3:00 pm. He arrived in Shanghai at around 6:00 pm that night. A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically went to the company yesterday morning to inquire about the results of this trip. According to him, this trip from Taiyuan to Xi'an was a direct flight, because the area is full of continuous mountains, so the flight was more difficult. The section from Xi'an to Xiangfan was covered in dense fog that day, so the flight was at an altitude of 3,500 feet. The sky was full of white clouds and Xiangfan was not visible, so it did not land. It has now been decided to start flights from next month, and to test the local climate route and add equipment at any time to ensure safety. In the future, if the weather is bad on the section from Beiping to Xi'an and it is inconvenient to fly directly over the mountains, then a test will be conducted from Beiping along the Beiping-Hankou Railway via Zhengding and then west, following the Zhengtai Railway to fly. From Taiyuan to Xi'an, the Fen River will be followed. However, the result is unpredictable.

The National Cement Federation Reiterates Relief Opinions 142

Cement Severely Affected by Doubled Unified Tax

Again Begging for the Withdrawal of the Order to Alleviate Difficulties

The National Cement Manufacturers Association believes that its business has been severely affected since the unified tax was doubled. It previously submitted a request to the Tax Department to find a way to cancel the tax payments that were made after the increase, but the Tax Department rejected it, stating that it was a general case. The Association submitted another request to the Tax Department yesterday, listing the difficulties of the business and requesting a way to remedy the situation. The original request is as follows: The case is about the doubled unified tax severely impacting domestic cement, respectfully reiterating opinions, and again begging for adoption to provide relief. The case was investigated by the association before the unified tax rate was ordered to be doubled, which has caused extremely serious damage to domestic people's livelihood. Therefore, a request was submitted to your office to respectfully request the withdrawal of the order to alleviate the difficulties. Your approval No. 189 stated (omitted)... Upon receiving this, it was investigated that China's cement industry is still in its infancy. Apart from the major commercial ports, sales are inherently limited. Compared to

Times of unrest and impoverished people's livelihood, most construction is stagnant. Therefore, cement sales are particularly affected. The output of various factories is oversupplied. Although the increased tax amount is borne by consumers, as your approval states, users will inevitably seek alternatives except for absolutely necessary uses, due to the increased burden. Therefore, the stagnation of cement sales is expected. However, the request to withdraw the order was not granted. Under the approval, the association is hesitant. The association also knows that the government's increase in the tax rate this time is unavoidable. If there were not many obstacles, the association would be willing to reluctantly endure the difficulties. Considering that the impact of heavy taxes on sales is as described above, the more stagnant the sales, the higher the cost, which will make it more difficult for factories to maintain their operations, and the more dangerous the future of industry and people's livelihood. If the government is not requested to find other relief measures, the resulting harm will be unspeakable. The association feels the danger and dares to submit the following opinions for relief:

Extended Period for Tax Account Booking: Most of the cement produced by the companies is stored in warehouses or distributed for sale, not sold immediately. However, the tax must be paid first. Even for the goods purchased by customers, the unified tax that should be paid is paid in advance by the companies due to credit sales. After the tax increase, the advance payment is even greater, and the companies have great difficulty in turning around their funds. The approval stated that there is a tax account booking system for paying the unified tax. If the manufacturers can find a bank guarantee, they can be allowed to book the tax, so they will not be subject to the difficulty of paying the unified tax in advance. It is deeply appreciated that your office is considerate of the difficulties of the business. However, the traditional tax account booking system has very strict restrictions. All tax account bookings must be paid by the 25th of each month. In reality, the companies must recover the tax paid in advance from customers in installments at the earliest two to three months later. For goods stored in warehouses or distributed for sale, it depends on the market conditions, so the recovery of the advance payment will take even longer. Therefore, even with the tax account booking system, the companies still cannot avoid the difficulty of paying the tax in advance. It is dared to request that the tax booking period be extended to three months, so that the companies can slightly ease

the burden.

Restricting the Import of Foreign Cement: The import and dumping of foreign cement have been very large in recent years. Although the government increased the import tax last May to show restriction, according to the customs trade book, the import of cement last year still reached 800,000 to 900,000 barrels, including those imported after last May. Considering that domestic cement production is already oversupplied, sales will be reduced even more after the increase in the unified tax. In order to maintain the domestic industry, it is hoped that other relief measures will be taken for the domestic cement that is reduced in sales due to this tax increase. The proposed method of relief is to request the government to strictly restrict the import of foreign goods and to review and increase the import tax rate again, in order to gradually reduce the import of cement, so that the reduced sales of domestic products can be slightly offset.

Please Reward Domestic Cement Immediately: Domestic cement has no sales in terms of exports due to transportation difficulties and foreign competition. Now that domestic sales are difficult to maintain due to the increased unified tax, the surplus of domestic cement should be developed separately. Overseas Chinese in the Nanyang Islands are enthusiastic about promoting domestic goods.

Page 12

For example, overseas Chinese in the Dutch Indies also sent a telegram last October to purchase a large number of domestic cement, but the price offered was far below the cost of the companies, and the transaction could not be completed. As a result, Japanese goods were still used. The association's intention is to request the government to allocate all of the increased import tax in the previous article to be used for export cement subsidies, so that domestic cement can be sold as much as possible in the Nanyang region. The government has nothing to lose, and the domestic industry will benefit greatly.

Revision of the Refund of Heavy Taxes: It is clearly stipulated in the unified tax regulations and cement unified tax collection regulations that cement that has already paid taxes shall not be subject to any other taxes in the unified tax area. However, Guangdong Province must re-levy a university donation of 90 cents per barrel and a telephone donation of 45 cents per barrel, totaling 1.35 yuan, for imported cement, which exceeds the recently revised unified tax rate by 15 cents per barrel. It is heard that Guangdong Province will follow up with an increase after this central tax increase. However, the cement produced by factories such as Xicun in Guangdong Province is not taxed. If this continues, the association's sales in Guangdong Province will be completely cut off. The association has repeatedly appealed for correction to share the burden. Although the Ministry of Finance's tax letter No. 1697 stipulates that the original unified tax can be refunded in full, it is considered that there is no actual loss for the manufacturers. However, the amount of the heavy tax levied in Guangdong Province is very different from the original actual tax. If not in accordance with,

The full amount of the heavy tax levied should be refunded. It is still not enough to show fairness and avoid losses. This issue is not only related to the survival of the association's companies, but also has a profound impact on the national legal credibility. It is hoped that a speedy correction will be made, and that the heavy taxes levied in Guangdong Province will be fully refunded before the tax system is unified. If other provinces have heavy taxes that exceed the original unified tax, it should also be allowed to follow suit to provide relief. The above sections are all essential plans for rescuing the domestic cement industry. The interests of the association's companies are truly skin deep. The association has always felt painful. Now that the tax rate has been increased, it is even more difficult to pay the tax in advance and promote the products. Without the consideration of your office to plan together, it is truly not enough to save the difficulties and maintain the industry. Therefore, the association dares to continue to state the facts and begs for verification and compliance to comfort the public's expectations and be deeply grateful. Respectfully submitted to Xie, the Director of the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance.

The Association for the Maintenance of National Products Requests the Abolition of Special Taxes on Porcelain 143

The tax rate is extremely heavy, no different from Likin

Domestic products are in danger, please provide relief

The Association for the Maintenance of National Products of China submitted a document to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance, stating, "Recently, according to the Joint Association of Porcelain Merchants in Jingdezhen and various guild halls, the porcelain merchants and others recently read the Shanghai News on December 26, 1933, which published an order from the Executive Yuan's Rural Rehabilitation Committee to all people's groups in the country, stating in brief that, 'It has been decreed by the Executive Yuan that to rehabilitate the countryside, it is necessary to first abolish exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes, and to abolish exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes, it is especially necessary to have a detailed investigation. The central government and the people are starting anew, and a decision has been made early on. It is hoped that the people and various groups in all regions will, based on their actual observations, make detailed reports. This matter concerns the foundation of the country, and we look forward to it,' etc. After reading it, we see that the central government is concerned about the people's difficulties, clearing away abuses, and sparing no effort. The porcelain merchants and others see this telegram as if they were experiencing a cloudburst in a severe drought, or a patient meeting a good doctor. How can we not be grateful? The Jiangxi Provincial Government launched a post-banditry production and sales donation in 1932, and Jingdezhen porcelain was also included in the levy. This donation is a disguised Likin. The porcelain merchants and others immediately, based on the central government's explicit order issued on January 1, 1931, to permanently abolish Likin and all donations similar to Likin, repeatedly argued and repeatedly submitted to the central government's various Yuan and Ministries, which approved the issuance of orders to abolish it. However, the Jiangxi Provincial Government stated that during the bandit suppression period, military expenses were vast and difficult to abolish. The porcelain production and sales donation was changed to a special business tax on porcelain, and the porcelain merchants were responsible for contracting the annual amount of 440,000 yuan. At this time, the porcelain merchants and others were unable to bear the burden, but because the government was having difficulty raising funds, they had to comply with this intention and bear the pain, hoping to abolish it as soon as possible. However, more than a year has passed, and the tax is still the same. The suffering of the porcelain merchants and others is indescribable. At the end of last year, we submitted the details in writing to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry, requesting approval to order the abolition. Now, we will reiterate to your association the serious relationship between the collection of the special business tax on porcelain, the decline of industry and commerce, and the endangerment of national products, as well as the special circumstances of the urgent need to abolish the tax. Jingdezhen porcelain is a national product that has enjoyed a great reputation in our country for more than ten years. The porcelain merchants and others purchase and transport it here, on the one hand, to promote national products and avoid the outflow of rights, and on the other hand, to supply the daily necessities of the people in various provinces of our country. However, since many years, although there are no tariffs, we are affected by natural and man-made disasters and the dumping of foreign porcelain. Not only is foreign trade unable to stand, but even the domestic market is almost taken away. A glimmer of hope is on the verge of extinction. Moreover, with the addition of heavy donations and taxes, it is difficult for porcelain merchants to survive. This is the first reason why the special business tax on porcelain should be abolished. In the era of special taxes, the tax rate for daily necessities was 5% to 5.5%, luxury goods 7.5% to 10%, and luxury goods 12% to 17.5%. It was only collected once locally and could be used throughout the country. The porcelain merchants and others still felt it was harsh and difficult to bear. Now, the special business tax on porcelain is being held, and it is also being levied according to the special tax rate. It is a separate system in Jiangxi Province. When porcelain is transported to various provinces and ports, a business tax must be collected again, so the burden is heavier than in the era of special taxes. Think about it, if porcelain merchants buy porcelain with 100 yuan of capital, they must pay at least 20 to 30 yuan in special business tax on porcelain and business tax in various provinces and ports. Adding in transportation costs of about 30 yuan, 40 to 50 yuan has been lost invisibly with 100 yuan of capital, and it is difficult to hope that they will not lose their capital. Therefore, foreign porcelain takes advantage of the situation to encroach, and domestic porcelain is gradually declining. This is the second reason why the special business tax on porcelain should be abolished. In terms of production and sales of Jingdezhen porcelain last year, it plummeted compared to previous years due to the restrictions of donations and taxes. It is truly rare in decades, and the public is panicked. In addition, the recent Min Province coup has affected the situation. Porcelain merchants in various provinces lack purchasing power. However, seeing the difficulties of the times and feeling heartbroken, they have stopped buying from the kiln owners. Due to the accumulation of porcelain and the inability to transport it, they have stopped working. Many workers have lost their jobs, and the local market has become stagnant. Cries of hunger and cold are often heard. If it is not abolished in time, it is no different from draining the pond to catch fish and burning the forest to hunt. This is the third reason why the special business tax on porcelain should be abolished. Jingdezhen porcelain is made by hand, with the finest division of labor. Hundreds of thousands of workers rely on this for their livelihoods. If the porcelain industry goes bankrupt and cuts off the livelihood, these people with limited knowledge will inevitably take risks. Moreover, the area is adjacent to bandit areas, and hidden dangers are worrying. This is the fourth reason why the special business tax on porcelain should be abolished. Jingdezhen has been captured by bandits three times since 1930, and its vitality has been greatly damaged. After several years, it has not yet recovered. Industry and commerce are in extreme difficulties. Local gentry and merchants are seeking relief every day. However, the rise and fall of the market depend on the porcelain industry, and the development of the porcelain industry must first abolish donations and taxes and then gradually prosper. This is the fifth reason why the special business tax on porcelain should be abolished. Currently, the economic bankruptcy of rural areas and the decline of industry and commerce have become a common situation in our country. National products, porcelain in particular, are in a very dangerous situation. The wise authorities already have relief measures for national silk and tea, and they should especially maintain national porcelain to strengthen the country. Therefore, the Executive Yuan has resolutely decided to rehabilitate the countryside, with the abolition of exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes as a prerequisite, and has ordered the Rural Rehabilitation Committee to investigate all people's groups in the country. The porcelain merchants and others are fortunate to have survived. It is reasonable to submit the above details in writing to your Yuan (Ministry) for review and approval to abolish them, so as to alleviate the people's difficulties and consolidate the foundation of the country. We are overwhelmed with anxiety and await your orders."

Huang Shaoxiong Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning, Denies Being Sent to Xinjiang 144

Minister of Interior Huang Shaoxiong arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at about 7:00 AM on the night express train from Beijing. A Far East News reporter visited his residence on Xihans Road to ask about the central government's sending him to Xinjiang and the issue of Inner Mongolian autonomy. According to the discussion, the details are recorded as follows:

Denies Going to Xinjiang: Mr. Huang first denied to the reporter the rumor that the central government would send him to Xinjiang, saying that this was just a rumor and should not be believed. How can the chaos in Xinjiang Province be calmed down simply by sending someone there? The central government has not yet received an official report on the so-called "independence" movement of the Xinjiang Hui people. Reports say that the so-called "independent" government has disintegrated because the president, premier, and others have been forced to flee by the Donggan army. This is just their internal power struggle and is not something to be optimistic about. At this point, the reporter asked whether the central government would send Li Du, the former Commander-in-Chief of the Jilin Self-Defense Army. Mr. Huang replied that the rumors that the central government would send himself or General Li, or himself and General Li together, were all speculation. However, the central government will indeed establish a Xinjiang Construction Planning Committee, with himself as one of the members of the committee.

Inner Mongolian Autonomy: Then, regarding the issue of Inner Mongolian autonomy, the central government has recently held several meetings to discuss it, and there are generally no problems. The opinions of the representatives of the various princes are only differences in wording. As for Prince Yun's resignation from the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, this matter is not enough to be taken seriously by the general public.

Reform of the Provincial System: Finally, the reporter cited reports that the central government intends to first implement the reform of the provincial system in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, and Hubei provinces, and asked Mr. Huang about it. He replied that the central government is still carefully studying the implementation steps of the reform of the provincial system, and the reports are not accurate. Mr. Huang continued that the internal affairs are being greatly tightened due to funding problems, and personnel are being cut to save money.

The Ministry of Communications Orders the Reinstatement of Opportunistic Measures Against Uncertified Crew Members 147

The China Marine Engineers General Association of this city previously petitioned the Ministry of Communications for a thorough investigation because the Shanghai Maritime Administration did not take opportunistic measures against those who drove machinery without certificates and those who impersonated others. Yesterday, a Ministry of Communications instruction was received, stating, "It has been investigated that the Association previously submitted a request to the Shanghai Maritime Administration for not taking measures against those who drive machinery without certificates and those who impersonate others. The Ministry instructed and ordered the Bureau to investigate and reply. Now, according to the reply, the Ministry's Instruction No. 498 stated in brief that, 'According to the China Marine Engineers Association's petition, the Bureau did not take measures against marine engineers who do not have certificates and those who impersonate others, ordering to investigate and reply.' Upon investigation, Mao Jietang, the third engineer of the Longshan ship of the Sanbei Company, was dismissed from the Bureau and completed the registration procedures for employment. The original petition stated that he was impersonating others and should provide sufficient evidence for investigation. After replying to the Marine Engineers Association, the Bureau will review the crew list, and crew members without certificates who are not in the petition will be opportunistically eliminated, without ever making concessions. The crew members without certificates mentioned in the original petition are currently applying for certificates, such as Kikawa Kohei, the chief engineer of the Xinli ship, and have been informed by the Ministry. Sheng Yulu, the chief engineer, has obtained Chief Engineer Certificate No. 629 of Grade B. The Association's statement is a misunderstanding. Based on the previous reasons, the handling situation is hereby submitted for review and approval. In addition to the instructions, this order is hereby issued for your information. This order is issued on February 21, 1933, by Wei Jia Hua, Minister of Communications."

Residents of Dayang Bridge, Which Was Demolished by the Railway Bureau, Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday 148

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration needed to demolish the small wooden bridge east of Dayang Bridge to build a fence along Jiaotong Road, which caused opposition from merchants and residents of Panjiawan in the area. The details have been recorded in previous reports. Yesterday, the Railway Bureau ordered the Engineering Department to verify the situation, and the merchants and residents sent representatives to petition the Municipal Government yesterday morning. The details are recorded again as follows:

Railway Bureau Verification: The merchants in the area have jointly submitted a petition to the Railway Bureau, requesting that the demolition be avoided. The Railway Bureau ordered the Engineering Department to conduct a detailed survey of the traffic situation in the area yesterday and submit a report for review. If the demolition of the bridge does not cause much loss to the residents in the area, the Railway Bureau will implement it for the sake of the project.

Residents' Petition: Residents of Panjiawan are deeply afraid that the Railway Bureau will implement the demolition for the sake of the project. Therefore, at 10:00 AM yesterday, they sent representatives Sun Guifen, Wang Xiwu, Chen Yuxin, and others, carrying a petition to the Municipal Government, requesting that the Railway Bureau be asked to exempt the demolition of the bridge. Section Chief Huang of the Second Section received them and promised to report their intention to the Mayor and ask the Railway Bureau to find a way to preserve the bridge. The representatives were satisfied and left.

Petition to the Municipal Government: The petition states that the Railway Bureau is not familiar with the local situation and intends to demolish the small wooden bridge on the main road, obstructing traffic and affecting the market. We respectfully request that you verify and quickly consult with the Railway Bureau to preserve it in order to maintain the people's livelihood. The merchants have been able to develop their businesses and maintain the market in Dayang Bridge because this small wooden bridge can pass through the railway to Panjiawan in the south. More than 10,000 citizens travel back and forth every day. Therefore, the Dayang Bridge and Panjiawan areas have the prosperity of commerce and industry today. The wooden bridge was noticed by the previous Director and was reserved. Now, the Railway Bureau has not carefully examined the local situation and will demolish the wooden bridge, blocking traffic. The livelihood of thousands of small industrialists and merchants will inevitably be in a desperate situation, which is related to the people's livelihood and has a huge impact. We repeatedly request preservation, but it has not been approved. The matter concerns local interests, and we have no choice but to publicly elect representatives to cry to the court. We respectfully ask you to sympathize with the people's difficulties and quickly consult with the Railway Bureau to preserve the wooden bridge or make it into a gate, so that people can freely travel back and forth to maintain local commerce, which is a great benefit.

The Postal and Remittance Talents of the Ministry of Communications for Studying in Austria, The Postal and Remittance Associations Electrically Asked the Ministry for Questions 149

and Expresses Opinions

It was reported that the Ministry of Communications intends to recruit trainees to study storage and remittance business directly in Austria in order to train talents in savings and remittance business. Upon hearing this news, the Postal and Remittance Associations specially sent a telegram to the Ministry of Communications to inquire about the truth and express their opinions. The following is a record of the telegram: Zhu Xun, Minister of Communications of Nanjing,

With respect, it is reported that your Ministry intends to recruit six trainees to study in Guangdong in order to train specialized talents in postal savings and remittance business, and will first be sent by the Postal and Savings Bureaus to designated domestic bureaus for two months of study, and then to Austria, with a setting-up fee of 3,000 yuan, round-trip travel expenses of 960 pounds, and monthly living expenses of 120 pounds, etc. Upon reading it, we were shocked. Regardless of the expenses borne by the people in this method, which should not be borne by the current postal service, which is constantly experiencing financial difficulties as your Ministry has often reported, there are already several people studying in Austria among the current service personnel in the post office, and there is no shortage of other specialized savings and remittance talents. If your Ministry needs savings and remittance talents, it only needs to select them according to the postal examination system, and there is no one who is not competent. This time, another recruitment outline for trainees has been formulated, and the qualifications stipulated are mostly inconsistent with the qualifications of our existing postal personnel. Once external recruitment is conducted, all postal employees will be rejected. This method clearly violates the inherent perfect examination system of the postal service, buries the existing specialized talents of the postal service, and the result will be that your Ministry's actions will gradually lead to the destruction of the postal system and the insertion of private individuals, to the waste of public funds, and especially to other matters. In order to maintain the postal system, our association and others deeply hope that this move is still a newspaper rumor and not a fact. We hereby send a special telegram to your Ministry to inquire about the details. If this is the case, we urge you to reconsider and withdraw the order. It would be a great blessing for the postal service. Shanghai Postal Workers Union, Shanghai Postal Staff Union, respectfully.

Customs Patrol Boats "Haiqing" and "Haicheng" Launched Yesterday 150

Bottle Broken by the Commissioner of Customs' Wife

The two patrol boats, "Haiqing" and "Haicheng," built by the Jiangnan Shipyard for the Jianghai Customs, were launched one after the other yesterday morning at around 10 a.m. Mrs. Fang Jiaju, wife of the Customs Commissioner, broke the bottles. Details are recorded below:

A Glimpse of the Ceremony Platform: In front of the "Haiqing" and "Haicheng" patrol boats, a ceremony platform of about twenty feet square and ten feet high was erected for each. The platform was covered with flags of all nations. In the center was a large flower vase presented by the shipyard to Mrs. Fang, who would break the bottles. At the bow of each patrol boat, a bottle of champagne was wrapped in five-colored silk ribbons. The national flag, with a white sun on a blue sky over a red earth, was hung fore and aft of the ships.

Chinese and Foreign Guests: Yesterday, those who attended the ceremony were welcomed from the Jianghai Customs pier by a small steamer specially prepared by the Jiangnan Shipyard. Those in attendance included Mr. Frand, Inspector of the Customs Patrol; Mr. Tailai, Superintendent of Works; Mr. Yuan Jin, Customs Commissioner; Mrs. Fang Jiaju, who would break the bottles; Commander Wang Shouting of the Naval Training Fleet; Mr. Wu Zhennan, Director of the Coast Guard; Commander Qiu Zizhong of the Yixian ship; Mr. Chen Zaofan, Deputy Director of the shipyard; Mr. Mao Gen, Chief Engineer; Mr. Liang Xunying, Head of the Materials Section; Mr. Yu Jianfu, Head of the Business Section; Mr. Ye Fangzhe, Head of the Statistics Section; Mr. Ye Baoqi, Battalion Commander of the Guard; and the captains of various ships stationed in Shanghai, etc.

Grand Launching Ceremony: At 10 a.m. sharp, the launching ceremony began. Mrs. Fang, who was to break the bottle, held a bouquet of fresh flowers in her left hand and a bottle of champagne hanging at the bow of the "Haiqing" patrol boat in her right hand. She aimed at the bow of the ship and threw the bottle with force. It hit the bow squarely, the bottle shattered, and champagne spilled everywhere. The guests attending the ceremony applauded in unison. The "Haiqing" ship was then launched into the Huangpu River, and two small boats specially dispatched by the shipyard towed the ship to the shipyard's pier to moor. At 10:30 a.m., Mrs. Fang broke the bottle for the "Haicheng" ship in the same manner, and the ceremony concluded. All the guests were invited by Directors Yu and Lin to the shipyard's restaurant for refreshments. Construction of the Two Ships: According to Mr. Yu Jianfu, head of the Business Section of the shipyard, speaking to a reporter from the Hua Dong News Agency, the two ships are 136 feet long, 25 feet wide, 11 feet deep, with a draft of 8 feet, a speed of 12 nautical miles, and equipped with two 3-pounder cannons, four machine guns, two steam engines, two smoke tube boilers, one short-wave radio, and one motorboat. The interior equipment is quite complete. Several more ships will also be launched one after another soon.

The Taxation Department Issues an Order to Cancel the Method of Converting and Packaging Local Wine in Jiangsu Province

An Order Was Issued Yesterday to the Unified Tax Bureau of the Three Provinces, etc.

The Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance, believing that the method of converting and packaging local wine in Jiangsu Province for taxation purposes was inconsistent with the current situation, issued a special order yesterday to the Unified Tax Bureau of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Districts and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau of Tobacco and Alcohol to immediately issue an order to cancel it and to instruct the industry to comply. The original text is as follows: After investigation, the conversion and packaging of local wine was originally intended to facilitate the sale of goods by merchants. In July, when the fixed tax on local wine was first implemented, the department approved nine locations in Jiangsu Province—Jiangning, Zhenjiang, Shangbao, Wuxi, Wujin, Taixian, Nantong, Wuxian, and Tongshan—as conversion locations, and ordered the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Tax Bureau and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau of Tobacco and Alcohol to comply with the record. In the past six months, the department has observed the situation, and only in Taixian has there been a misunderstanding due to conversion. Taixing and Taixian are both places of origin of Su-style liquor, and their brewing methods and sales situations are largely the same. The production volume of Taixian is not even as great as that of Taixing, and the liquor transported from Taixing is not converted at the place of origin and has not encountered any difficulties. Now, the farmers in Taixian who produce liquor have also been approved by the bureau to send liquor for taxation using thin books, which is already a great convenience for merchants and has no need to apply the conversion method. All the aforementioned approval of the Taixian local wine conversion area should be immediately canceled to eliminate malpractices and avoid disputes. In addition to separate orders to the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Tax Bureau and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau of Tobacco and Alcohol, this order is also issued to the bureau, so that the Taidong Tobacco and Alcohol Branch Bureau and the Taixian Inspection Branch will comply. From the date of the order, conversion will be stopped immediately. The bureau will also jointly announce to merchants with the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Tax Bureau and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau of Tobacco and Alcohol so that everyone is aware of it. The situation of compliance will be reported for verification. In addition, if there are any conversion incidents in the place of origin, it should also be investigated and reported for approval and cancellation. This order.

Rice Merchants' Meeting Declares That Dumping of Japanese Rice is Japanese Counter-Propaganda

Attempting to Disrupt the Domestic Rice Market Price and Take the Opportunity to Buy

The Matter Concerns the Rural Economy; Advise the Industry to Strictly Prevent It

The news of the dumping of Japanese rice in China has been repeatedly reported in various newspapers. The rice merchant community in this city is particularly concerned because it is directly related to their business. After sending personnel to investigate in various directions, it was determined that this was Japanese counter-propaganda, attempting to disrupt the domestic rice market price. A special meeting was held yesterday to formally declare this. The details are as follows:

Japanese Side Fabricates Rumors: The Bean and Rice Industry Association of this city, before the meeting, saw news reports of a large amount of Japanese rice being shipped to China and dumped, which caused extreme panic. Because the price of domestic rice fell sharply last year, the rural economy went bankrupt and was beyond recovery. If Japanese rice were to be dumped again, the domestic market would become even more chaotic. Therefore, they paid serious attention and sent personnel to various customs offices and foreign firms in the city to conduct investigations. Yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m., a special meeting was convened, attended by more than 20 executive and supervisory committee members. The investigators first reported the results of their investigations, stating that this matter was entirely Japanese counter-propaganda, attempting to shake the domestic rice market. Subsequently, the entire body resolved to formally issue a statement to expose the Japanese conspiracy and to warn the industry.

Buying Chinese Rice: According to Mr. Zhu Zixiang, a standing committee member of the Bean and Rice Industry Association, the shipping and dumping of Japanese rice in China has been verified as a Japanese "air operation." The market situation of the Japanese rice industry is such that the price of rice is, on average, more than ten yuan per picul. If it were shipped to China and dumped, our country has already implemented a new tax on rice and wheat imports, which, together with miscellaneous expenses, would total no less than eighteen yuan per stone. The purpose of the Japanese side's counter-propaganda this time is to cause the price of our domestic rice to plummet, on the one hand, causing rural bankruptcy, which would be even more irreparable, and on the other hand, taking the opportunity to buy Chinese rice and ship it to Japan to replenish their warehouses in preparation for extraordinary events. This kind of cunning tactic is not difficult to discern. Therefore, the entire industry has decided on preventive measures to avoid falling into their trap.
